1439102724|5.0|Sing me Home is another great novel that takes a current moral and political issue and gives it a story that so many will relate to. In the beginning of the book your heart breaks for Zoe, a music therapist who wants a child so badly, and has a terrible miscarriage. Her husband Max, who also has fertility issues, cannot afford any more of the IVF or the emotional consequences of all their failed attempts at having children. This leads to the dissolving of their marriage and Max, a recovering alcoholic turns to drinking to cope with the loss. Zoe then meets Vanessa, a counselor at a local high school who requests music therapy for one of her students. The two become close friends, and eventually realize their feelings are more then just friendship. After getting married in another state, Zoe and Vanessa decide that they would like to have children, however Zoe has had a hysterectomy and cannot carry a child. She does however have an embryo left from her prior IVF with Max and she decides to get the embryo implanted in Vanessa. When she goes to Max to make the request he is living with his conservative brother who is a member of a church that has strong opinions against homosexuality and he decides to deny their request and instead asks that he get the embryo to \\"give\\" to his brother and his wife who have also been unsuccessful at having kids. This begins a legal battle that brings in a character of a lawyer that is provided by the church to help make a political statement and spectacle over their \\"custody\\" dispute. Throughout the trial Max grows closer to his brother's wife, and realizes that he is in love with her and that is the main influence on his decision to give them the embryo. The trial takes a toll on both Max and Zoe, and in the end the judge rules for the embryo to be given to Max. He does the right thing and promptly hands it over to Zoe, and in the end they have formed a mixed family around their daughter. This is another one of those books that makes you think about what you would do in a given situation, and is beautifully written from the many perspectives that Jodi Piccoult is known for. This is a must read book.<br /><br />Book Rating: 5/5<br />Book Received From: Atria / Simon & Schuster for Review<br />Reviewer: Gabi for Book Sakeyou think about what you would do in a given situation, and is beautifully written from the many perspectives that Jodi Piccoult is known for. B003HE2B6C|3.0|[ 2 1/2 Stars ] This isn't the worst thing I've ever heard; however, being that it was released after the likes of \\"This Time Around,\\" \\"Underneath,\\" and the \\"Stand Up, Stand Up\\" EP, it leaves a lot to be desired. It's not the songs are necessarily bad, it's just that they're not Hanson's most inspired work. I haven't been particularly fond of their more recent releases (post TTA) largely because the more recent albums are lacking thematically as they show no signs of musical growth. 2007's \\"The Walk\\" was preachy at best in its effort to be full of deep \\"obviously trying too hard\\" lyrical themes ..And when it wasn't trying too hard, it was otherwise just another batch of boring or moderately catchy, dismissible pop songs.     \\"This Time Around\\" managed to surprise even casual music listeners with a \\"wiser then their years\\" sense of maturity, and despite being thirteen the first time I heard this album, I knew they'd have a hard time bordering on the depth of songs like \\"This Time Around,\\" \\"A Song to Sing\\" and \\"Sure About It.\\" There were pop songs on this album, but it had enough substance to allow the songs with lighter themes to blend in with and be carried by the wider range in lyrical content.      \\"Underneath\\" is otherwise forgettable minus songs like \\"Strong Enough To Break,\\" \\"Underneath,\\" \\"Believe,\\" \\"Hey\\" and of course, \\"Penny and Me.\\" \\"Penny and Me\\" can easily be dismissed as a poppy summer song, but it lends itself well to a multitude of interpretations. \\"Penny and Me\\" was the potential comeback song that wasn't promoted properly. \\"Underneath\\" and \\"Shout It Out\\" are similar in that there are some memorable songs, but the rest of the songs are otherwise forgettable, mediocre, or catchy at best.      I know \\"Shout It Out\\" is obviously a pop album, but it's arguably more poppy (and more juvenile) than \\"Middle Of Nowhere.\\" It's an improvement compared to \\"The Walk\\" as it makes no consolation or secret of the fact that it's pop music. Despite the record's honesty,it still leaves something to be desired. There are some stand-out songs though: \\"These Walls\\" (though I liked the \\"Stand Up, Stand Up\\" EP version much better), \\"Voice In The Chorus\\" (despite being an acquired taste, I respect what they were trying to do with this song), \\"Use Me Up,\\" \\"Carry You There,\\" and \\"Me, Myself and I\\" (which is a slightly less inspired version of \\"A Song To Sing\\"). The horn section winds up making most of the songs sound like some half-fast 70s knock off. \\"Thinking 'bout Something\\" is okay, and it's probably the only song that merits the horns. \\"Make It Out Alive,\\" \\"Musical Ride,\\" \\"Kiss Me When You Come Home,\\" and \\"Waiting for This\\" are okay, but they qualify more as tollerable filler than anything else. \\"Make It Out Alive\\" could've done without the horn section.       \\"And I Wanted\\" and \\"Give A Little\\" are so cheesy that a) I don't believe guys in their mid to late 20s wrote these songs and b) they dont even deserve a spot on the album. They're the kind of songs that make me wonder what fan base Hanson is trying to target and if they want these new fans to take them at all seriously. I have no idea what they were thinking when they decided to release \\"Give A Little.\\" All in all, Hanson has shown me that their definition of the word \\"pop\\" is synonymous with derivative laughable crap. The album was apparently supposed to sound like \\"World's On Fire,\\" and I'm not quite sure where they lost sight of that. I understand what sound they were going for with \\"Shout It Out,\\" but for whatever reason, it wound up getting lost in translation by being taken that one step too far. They should leave their stiflingly rigid interpretation of bubblegum pop music for a band like \\"Tinted Windows.\\"        Between \\"Underneath,\\" \\"The Walk,\\" and \\"Shout It Out,\\" the good songs on each respective album can make for one decent album. If you're new to Hanson, start out with \\"TTA,\\" the \\"Middle of Nowhere Acoustic\\" re-recording from 2007, or \\"Underneath,\\" and work your way around from there. Try to fish around for some unreleased tunes and b-sides. These songs showcase Hanson's versatility; Hanson is at their best when they're not constricted by their own self-imposed constraints. Rather than conforming to the more cohessive stylings of a particular album's sound, their unreleased material really allows listeners to get a sense of Hanson's true potential and versatility.     I would've given this album a 2 and a half star rating if I could've. I wish the insightful Hanson would come back.. I don't need guys who are pushing 30 to bust around doing some gimmicky blues brothers pastiche. TTA was \\"no nonsense\\" pop-rock at its best, and they slowly started going downhill after that.
B000E1ZBGS|5.0|Jane Austen affected a sea change in the novel in the early 1800s. Before that time the novel was limited to rather farfetched adventure stories like Daniel Defoe's Robinson Crusoe. In the early 19th century, writing about everyday events was quite out of the ordinary, and Jane was the first to successfully portray the behind the scenes workings of the ladies and gentlemen of the English countryside.<br /><br />Watching a new adaptation of a Jane Austen novel is like seeing Shakespeare's Hamlet, there are no surprises in the final outcome. Rather the entertainment comes in the particular adaptation, actor's skills, and production qualities. Austen's Pride & Prejudice is one of her most popular novels, and each time it has found it's way onto the big screen and into DVD it's created a lot of passion for and against the adaptation.<br /><br />Universal's production has had a number of disappointed viewers as evidenced by many an online review. This disappointment typically seems to stem with having something to do with the casting decisions and the perceived lack of chemistry between the principal players. Conversely, some felt there was too much chemistry, or not enough propriety in the manner in which the Bennet's conducted themselves. Or that the Bennet's were incorrectly shown to be struggling financially and therefore didn't live or dress up to the idealized version of English gentility.<br /><br />To the chemistry of the actors, I believe the casting in Universal's version was excellent. Matthew Macfadyen perfectly portrayed the aloof, shy, yet emotionally caring Mr. Darcy. Keira Knightley is a surprise in this role, for she is able to capture the strong-willed, hastily opinionated and yet free spirited Elizabeth Bennet quite well. But more importantly, this adaptation develops the full picture of the Bennet Family, with all five Bennet girls, with their individual personalities vying for the best dress, or introduction. Both Brenda Blethyn as Mrs. Bennet, and Donald Sutherland as Mr. Bennet are superb in their timing, and comedic needling of one another. Judi Dench as the controlling Lady Catherine de Bourg, is pleasingly condescending wicked.<br /><br />Screenwriter Deborah Moggach portrayed the Bennet family in a very real and grounded environment. While she may have packaged Austen's novel in a less glamorous light than is typical; she was able to reflect the troubling circumstances people of that time had to deal with.  After all, the financial fix and worry of having five girls with no inheritance in 18th century England was the very point of view and experience that Jane wrote from.<br /><br />Between Director Wright and screenwriter Moggach, this version of Pride & Prejudice is deeply thought-provoking, and portrays the ups and down, moral questions, dilemmas, and hardships of being in society in the 18th century.. Bennet are superb in their timing, and comedic needling of one another. Judi Dench as the controlling Lady Catherine de Bourg, is pleasingly condescending wicked.    Screenwriter Deborah Moggach portrayed the Bennet family in a very real and grounded environment. While she may have packaged Austen's novel in a less glamorous light than is typical; she was able to reflect the troubling circumstances people of that time had to deal with.  After all, the financial fix and worry of having five girls with no inheritance in 18th century England was the very point of view and experience that Jane wrote from.     Between Director Wright and screenwriter Moggach, this version of Pride & Prejudice is deeply thought-provoking, and portrays the ups and down, moral questions, dilemmas, and hardships of being in society in the 18th century.
